CHAPTER ______
1 AN ACT concerning
2 Continuing the Next Generation Energy Act
3 Utility RELIEF (Reducing Energy Load Inflation for Everyday Families) Act
4 FOR the purpose of lowering the maximum monthly energy demand that is required for a
5 certain large load customer to qualify for a specific rate schedule; altering the
6 requirements that a certain multiyear rate plan must meet to be eligible for
7 approval; authorizing the Public Service Commission to require a public service
8 company to include a certain reconciliation procedure in the company’s multiyear
9 rate plan; altering the program cycle for certain energy efficiency and conservation
10 plans; altering the years for which certain electricity savings percentages are used
11 to calculate certain greenhouse gas emissions reduction targets in certain years;
12 prohibiting the Commission from approving a certain energy efficiency and
13 conservation plan that includes a certain residential sector subprogram; altering the
14 definition of “large capacity energy resource” and “zero–emission credit” for
15 provisions relating to energy solicitation and procurement; requiring the
16 Commission to consider, rather than apply, certain costs when calculating certain
17 impacts for certain nuclear energy generation projects; authorizing, with the
18 approval of the Commission, the increase of certain nuclear energy generation
19 project costs under certain circumstances; requiring the Commission to conduct a
20 certain request for information and a certain request for proposals; requiring the
21 Commission to select a certain third–party administrator by a certain date subject
22 to a certain exception; requiring the Power Plant Research Program, in consultation
23 with the Department of the Environment and the Maryland Energy Administration,

10 (a) (1) (I) [The Commission shall establish] THERE IS an electric

14 ELECTRIC UNIVERSAL SERVICE PROGRAM.
15 (III) THE PURPOSE OF THE ELECTRIC UNIVERSAL SERVICE
16 PROGRAM IS TO ASSIST ELECTRIC CUSTOMERS WITH ANNUAL INCOMES AT OR
17 BELOW 200% OF THE FEDERAL POVERTY LEVEL.

19 (i) bill assistance;
20 (ii) low–income residential weatherization; and
21 (iii) the retirement of arrearages for electric customers who have not
22 received assistance in retiring arrearages under the ELECTRIC universal service program

26 electric universal service program.

17 Article – Local Government
18 1–1320.
19 (a) (1) In this section the following words have the meanings indicated.
20 (2) “Administration” means the Maryland Energy Administration.
21 (3) “Residential energy storage system” means a system, on a residential
22 customer’s side of the meter, used to store electrical energy, or mechanical, chemical, or
23 thermal energy that was once electrical energy, for use as electrical energy at a later date
24 or in a process that offsets electricity use at peak times.
25 (4) “Residential solar energy system” means any configuration of solar
26 energy devices that collects and distributes solar energy for the purpose of generating
27 electricity and that has a single residential interconnection with the electrical grid.
28 (5) “SOLAR PERMITTING FEE” MEANS A FEE EQUAL TO THE SUM OF
29 ALL CHARGES IMPOSED BY A COUNTY OR MUNICIPALITY, INCLUDING CHARGES
30 IMPOSED BY A PROVIDER OF SOLAR PERMITTING SOFTWARE, IN CONNECTION WITH
31 AN APPLICATION FOR A RESIDENTIAL SOLAR ENERGY SYSTEM.
32 (6) “Solar permitting software” means[:
HOUSE BILL 1532 15
1 (i) the most recent version of a web–based platform, developed by
2 the National Renewable Energy Laboratory, that provides a standard portal for receiving
3 and processing residential solar energy system and residential energy storage system
4 permit information; or
5 (ii) automated software that functions to support the tracking and
6 approval of residential building permits for residential solar energy systems, residential
7 energy storage systems, main electrical panel upgrades, and main electrical panel devices]
8 SOFTWARE OR A COMBINATION OF SOFTWARE THAT:
9 (I) AUTOMATES PLAN REVIEW FOR RESIDENTIAL SOLAR
10 ENERGY SYSTEMS TO THE MOST RECENT VERSION OF, AS APPLICABLE:
11 1. THE MARYLAND BUILDING PERFORMANCE

25 (a) (1) There is an Environmental Trust Fund.

28 surcharge per kilowatt hour of electric energy distributed in the State to be paid by any
29 electric company as defined in § 1–101 of the Public Utilities Article.
30 (ii) The Public Service Commission shall impose the surcharge per
31 kilowatt hour of electric energy distributed to retail electric customers within the State and
32 shall authorize the electric companies to add the full amount of the surcharge to retail
33 electric customers’ bills.
HOUSE BILL 1532 19
1 (iii) To the extent that the surcharge is not collected from retail
2 electric customers, the surcharge shall be deemed a cost of distribution and shall be allowed

15 fiscal year 2030.

18 (ii) has or is projected to have a load factor of over [80%] 75%.
19 (4) “Load ramp period” means the period of time from commencement of
20 service until a large load customer’s billing calculation is based on the full contract capacity.
21 (b) It is the intent of the General Assembly that residential retail electric
22 customers in the State should not bear the financial risks associated with large load
23 customers interconnecting to the electric system serving the State.

1 (2) protects residential retail electric customers from the financial risks

19 2. deploy energy storage devices in a cost–effective manner;

26 guarantees, and other similar benefits as the benefits become available; or

10 7–321.
11 (A) IN THIS SECTION, “PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM”
12 MEANS A MOVABLE PHOTOVOLTAIC SOLAR ENERGY GENERATION DEVICE THAT IS:
13 (1) DESIGNED TO BE CONNECTED TO A BUILDING’S ELECTRICAL
14 SYSTEM THROUGH A STANDARD ELECTRICAL OUTLET;
15 (2) PRIMARILY INTENDED TO OFFSET PART OF THE BUILDING’S
16 ELECTRICITY CONSUMPTION;
17 (3) LIMITED TO SUPPLYING A MAXIMUM POWER OUTPUT OF NOT
18 MORE THAN 391 WATTS BACK TO THE ELECTRIC SYSTEM OF THE BUILDING; AND
19 (4) CERTIFIED BY UNDERWRITERS LABORATORY OR AN EQUIVALENT
20 NATIONALLY RECOGNIZED TESTING LABORATORY.
21 (B) A PERSON MAY PURCHASE AND INSTALL NOT MORE THAN ONE
22 PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM PER ELECTRIC METER FOR
23 RESIDENTIAL USE ONLY.
24 (C) A PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM:
25 (1) IS NOT SUBJECT TO THE REQUIREMENTS OF §§ 7–306 AND 7–306.1
26 OF THIS SUBTITLE;
27 (2) IS NOT ELIGIBLE FOR INCLUSION IN MEETING THE RENEWABLE
28 ENERGY PORTFOLIO STANDARD; AND
29 (3) MAY NOT GENERATE RENEWABLE ENERGY CREDITS OF ANY TYPE.
HOUSE BILL 1532 57
1 (D) AN ELECTRIC COMPANY:
2 (1) MAY NOT REQUIRE A CUSTOMER USING A PORTABLE SOLAR
3 ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM TO:
4 (I) OBTAIN THE ELECTRIC COMPANY’S APPROVAL BEFORE
5 INSTALLING OR USING THE PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM;
6 (II) PAY ANY FEE OR CHARGE RELATED TO THE PORTABLE
7 SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM’S ABILITY TO FEED ELECTRICITY BACK INTO
8 THE ELECTRIC SYSTEM; OR
9 (III) EXCEPT AS PROVIDED IN SUBSECTION (E) OF THIS SECTION,
10 INSTALL ANY ADDITIONAL CONTROLS OR EQUIPMENT BEYOND WHAT IS
11 INTEGRATED INTO THE PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM; AND
12 (2) IS NOT LIABLE FOR ANY DAMAGE CAUSED BY A PORTABLE SOLAR
13 ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM.
14 (E) A CUSTOMER USING A PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM
15 SHALL:
16 (1) NOTIFY THE ELECTRIC COMPANY PROVIDING SERVICE IN THE
17 SERVICE TERRITORY IN WHICH THE GENERATING SYSTEM WILL BE INSTALLED ONCE
18 THE GENERATING SYSTEM IS INSTALLED;
19 (2) PROVIDE TO THE ELECTRIC COMPANY PROVIDING SERVICE IN
20 THE SERVICE TERRITORY IN WHICH THE GENERATING SYSTEM WILL BE OR IS
21 INSTALLED A CERTIFICATION OF THE SAFETY FEATURES AND MAXIMUM
22 GENERATING CAPACITY OF THE GENERATING SYSTEM; AND
23 (3) IF THE GENERATING SYSTEM REQUIRES AN AUTOMATIC LOCKING
24 DISCONNECT SWITCH TO BE INSTALLED, PAY FOR THE SWITCH INSTALLATION.

5 automatically on the earlier of:
6 (i) the last day of the fiscal year for which money last was
7 appropriated; or
8 (ii) the date provided in the termination clause of the procurement
9 contract.

12 (i) incurred as a result of the multi–year contract; but

11 RENEWABLE ENERGY SOURCES COLLECTIVELY.
12 (B) (1) THE ADMINISTRATION, IN CONSULTATION WITH THE
13 COMMISSION, SHALL DEVELOP AND CONDUCT THE AUCTIONS IN A MANNER THAT IS
14 COST–EFFECTIVE AND MAINTAINS AND PROMOTES THE DEVELOPMENT OF
15 RENEWABLE ENERGY IN THE STATE.
16 (2) THE COMPETITIVE AUCTION PROCESS MAY REQUIRE THE
17 ADMINISTRATION TO SOLICIT A SERIES OF BIDS FROM RENEWABLE ENERGY
18 PROJECT DEVELOPERS FOR THE DEVELOPMENT OF RENEWABLE ENERGY
19 GENERATION PROJECTS THAT ARE NEEDED TO MEET ELECTRICITY DEMAND IN A
20 COST–EFFECTIVE MANNER.
21 (C) (1) TO BE ELIGIBLE TO SUBMIT A BID UNDER THIS SECTION, A
22 PERSON MUST:
23 (I) BE A RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT
24 DEVELOPER; AND
25 (II) MEET THE MINIMUM CREDIT AND OTHER ELIGIBILITY
26 REQUIREMENTS SET UNDER PARAGRAPH (2) OF THIS SUBSECTION.
27 (2) THE ADMINISTRATION, IN CONSULTATION WITH THE
28 COMMISSION, SHALL SET ELIGIBILITY REQUIREMENTS FOR BIDDERS, INCLUDING
29 REQUIRING EACH BIDDER TO:
30 (I) PROVIDE PROOF OF FINANCIAL INTEGRITY;
HOUSE BILL 1532 75
1 (II) POST A BOND OR OTHER SIMILAR INSTRUMENT;
2 (III) AGREE TO BE SUBJECT TO ALL APPLICABLE TAXES; AND
3 (IV) COMPLY WITH ANY OTHER REQUIREMENTS THE
4 ADMINISTRATION DETERMINES ARE IN THE PUBLIC INTEREST.
5 (D) (1) ELIGIBLE BIDDERS SHALL SUBMIT COMPETITIVE BIDS BY
6 SPECIFYING:
7 (I) THE ACTUAL AMOUNT OF MEGAWATTS TO BE GENERATED
8 BY THE RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT; AND
9 (II) A PRICE PER MEGAWATT THAT WOULD BE REQUIRED FROM
10 THE AUCTION.
11 (2) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL RANK BIDS FROM LOWEST TO
12 HIGHEST COST PER MEGAWATT AND AWARD FUNDS DERIVED FROM ALTERNATIVE
13 COMPLIANCE FEES TO THE LOWEST BID OR BIDS.
14 (3) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL AWARD BIDS UNTIL THE CAPACITY
15 TARGET SET UNDER SUBSECTION (A)(2) OF THIS SECTION IS REACHED.
16 (4) THE BIDDER WHO SUBMITS THE LOWEST RESPONSIVE BID FOR
17 DEVELOPING A RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT SHALL BE AWARDED
18 THE AMOUNT OF FUNDS TO BUILD THE RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT.
19 (5) THE ADMINISTRATION MAY REFUSE TO ACCEPT SOME OR ALL OF
20 THE BIDS MADE IN A COMPETITIVE AUCTION IN ACCORDANCE WITH STANDARDS
21 ADOPTED BY THE ADMINISTRATION.
22 (6) (I) IF THE CAPACITY TARGET CAN BE MET AT A COST BELOW
23 THE ALLOCATED FUNDING, THE ADMINISTRATION MAY:
24 1. CARRY FORWARD ANY FUNDING TO THE NEXT
25 AUCTION, IF APPLICABLE; OR
26 2. APPLY THE FUNDS FOR ANY ADDITIONAL MEGAWATTS
27 OF RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION THAT HAVE BEEN OFFERED UNDER THE
28 AUCTION.
29 (II) ANY AMOUNT OF ALLOCATED FUNDING THAT IS NOT
30 CARRIED FORWARD OR APPLIED UNDER SUBPARAGRAPH (I) OF THIS PARAGRAPH
76 HOUSE BILL 1532
1 SHALL ACCRUE IN THE MARYLAND STRATEGIC ENERGY INVESTMENT FUND AND
2 MAY BE ALLOCATED FOR ANY PURPOSE FOR WHICH ALTERNATIVE COMPLIANCE FEE
3 REVENUE IS AUTHORIZED TO BE USED.
4 (E) (1) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL SET DELIVERY DEADLINES FOR
5 EACH RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT THAT IS AWARDED FUNDING
6 FROM AN AUCTION.
7 (2) THE DEADLINES SET IN PARAGRAPH (1) OF THIS SUBSECTION
8 SHALL INCLUDE MILESTONES THAT REQUIRE THE DEVELOPER TO MEET CERTAIN
9 DELIVERY GOALS DURING THE DEVELOPMENT OF A RENEWABLE ENERGY
10 GENERATION PROJECT.
11 (3) THE ADMINISTRATION MAY GRANT EXTENSIONS FOR DELIVERY
12 GOALS THAT ARE DELAYED DUE TO INTERCONNECTION OR PERMITTING
13 CHALLENGES OR DELAYS IF THE DEVELOPER PROVIDES DOCUMENTATION OF THE
14 CHALLENGE OR DELAY.
15 (4) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL ESTABLISH A METHOD OF
16 COLLECTION AGAINST ANY DEVELOPER AWARDED A CONTRACT UNDER THIS
17 SECTION TO RECAPTURE ANY FUNDS RECEIVED AS A RESULT OF:
18 (I) MISAPPROPRIATION, OVERPAYMENT, OR FRAUD; OR
19 (II) FAILURE TO MEET MILESTONES OR DELIVERY DATES.
20 (F) WITHIN 90 DAYS AFTER ALL CONTRACTS FOR RENEWABLE ENERGY
21 GENERATION PROJECTS ARE EXECUTED, THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL PUBLICLY
22 DISCLOSE THE NAMES OF EACH SUCCESSFUL BIDDER AND THE MEGAWATTS TO BE
23 DELIVERED BY THE DEVELOPMENT OF THE RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION
24 PROJECT.
25 (G) ON OR BEFORE JULY 1, 2027, AND JULY 1, 2028, THE ADMINISTRATION
26 AND THE COMMISSION SHALL REPORT TO THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY, IN
27 ACCORDANCE WITH § 2–1257 OF THIS ARTICLE, ON THE ADMINISTRATION OF THE
28 IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING AUCTION, INCLUDING:
29 (1) THE AMOUNT OF MEGAWATTS PROCURED THROUGH THE
30 AUCTION;
31 (2) THE COST PER MEGAWATT OF RENEWABLE ENERGY ALLOCATED
32 IN THE AUCTION;
HOUSE BILL 1532 77
1 (3) THE NUMBER OF RENEWABLE ENERGY CREDITS CREATED AS A
2 RESULT OF THE AUCTION; AND
3 (4) ANY OTHER INFORMATION THE ADMINISTRATION AND THE
4 COMMISSION CONSIDER RELEVANT.
5 (H) THE ADMINISTRATION, IN CONSULTATION WITH THE COMMISSION,
6 SHALL ADOPT REGULATIONS TO CARRY OUT THIS SECTION.

7 (a) (1) IN THIS SECTION THE FOLLOWING WORDS HAVE THE MEANINGS

9 (2) (I) “BONUS” MEANS A FORM OF DIRECT OR INDIRECT

11 EMPLOYEE OF A PUBLIC SERVICE COMPANY IN ADDITION TO THE EMPLOYEE’S BASE
12 PAY.
13 (II) “BONUS” INCLUDES:
14 1. COMPENSATION THAT THE PUBLIC SERVICE
15 COMPANY DOES NOT FORMALLY LABEL AS A BONUS PAYMENT;
16 2. ANY FORM OF INCENTIVE COMPENSATION THE FACT
17 AND AMOUNT OF WHICH IS UNDER THE DISCRETION OF THE PUBLIC SERVICE
18 COMPANY UNTIL A TIME CLOSE TO THE END OF THE PERIOD FOR WHICH THE
19 INCENTIVE PAYMENT IS PAID; AND
20 3. PAYMENTS GIVEN IN ADDITION TO BASE PAY THAT
21 ARE CONTINGENT ON THE OCCURRENCE OF ONE OR MORE EVENTS OR CONDITIONS.

21 (1) INCREASES BENEFITS TO RATEPAYERS BY LOWERING ELECTRIC

30 METERING PROGRAM UNDER § 7–306 OF THIS SUBTITLE.

11 (5) to meet the total statewide long–term pricing purchase obligation for
12 all applications approved in an order issued under § 7–1217 of this subtitle, require the
13 Commission to annually establish each electric company’s zero–emission credit purchase
14 obligation based on the most recent final electricity sales data as reported by PJM
15 Interconnection and measured at the customer’s meter in proportion to the electric
16 company’s share of statewide load.
17 (c) (1) Each electric company shall procure from the escrow account
18 established by regulation under this section a quantity of zero–emission credits equal to
19 the electric company’s respective percentage of retail electric sales each year.
20 (2) Subject to any escrow account reserve requirement the Commission
21 establishes, if there are insufficient zero–emission credits available to satisfy the electric
22 companies’ zero–emission credit purchase obligations, the overpayment shall be distributed
23 to electric companies to be refunded or credited to each distribution customer based on the
24 customer’s consumption of electricity supply that is subject to the renewable energy
25 portfolio standard.
26 (d) A debt, an obligation, or a liability of a nuclear energy generation project or of
27 an owner or operator of a nuclear energy generation project may not be considered a debt,
28 an obligation, or a liability of the State.
29 (E) (1) SUBJECT TO PARAGRAPH (2) OF THIS SUBSECTION, THE
30 COMMISSION MAY APPROVE AN INCREASE OF THE TOTAL COST OF A NUCLEAR
31 ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT UNDER A LONG–TERM PRICING PURCHASE
32 OBLIGATION.
33 (2) THE TOTAL COST OF A NUCLEAR ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT
34 UNDER A LONG–TERM PRICING PURCHASE OBLIGATION MAY NOT BE INCREASED BY
35 MORE THAN 15% OF THE ORIGINAL COST.
HOUSE BILL 1532 103
1 SECTION 2. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
2 (a) (1) On or before July 1, 2026, the Public Service Commission shall issue a
3 request for information on the use of a third–party, single–implementer program for the
4 administration of the programs and services under Title 7, Subtitle 2, Part II of the Public
5 Utilities Article.
6 (2) The request for information shall seek:
7 (i) determinations of what effect the use of a single, third–party
8 administrator would have on costs;
9 (ii) identification of technical and logistical barriers to transitioning
10 to a single, third–party administrator; and
11 (iii) an analysis of the advantages and disadvantages of a private,
12 third–party administrator as opposed to a State administrator.
13 (3) The request for information shall specify a completion date of July 1,
14 2027.
15 (b) (1) Within 30 days after receiving the information requested in subsection
16 (a) of this section, the Public Service Commission shall issue a request for proposals for a
17 third–party administrator for the programs and services under Title 7, Subtitle 2, Part II
18 of the Public Utilities Article.
19 (2) The request for proposals shall specify that responses to the request
20 should minimize short–term and long–term costs for utility ratepayers.
21 (c) (1) Except as provided in paragraph (2) of this subsection, on or before June
22 1, 2028, the Public Service Commission shall select, through the request for proposals
23 process initiated under subsection (b) of this section, a third–party administrator for the
24 administration of the programs and services under Title 7, Subtitle 2, Part II of the Public
25 Utilities Article.
26 (2) (i) The Public Service Commission may decline to select a
27 third–party administrator if the Public Service Commission determines that the use of a
28 third–party administrator would not be cost effective.
29 (ii) The Public Service Commission shall notify the General
30 Assembly of a decision to decline to select a third–party administrator within 5 days after
31 making the decision.
32 SECTION 3. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
33 (a) The Power Plant Research Program, in consultation with the Department of
34 the Environment and the Maryland Energy Administration, shall conduct a study to
104 HOUSE BILL 1532
1 identify ways to streamline the permitting process for energy development in the State.
2 (b) In conducting the study under subsection (a) of this section, the Power Plant
3 Research Program shall:
4 (1) identify up to 50 priority energy sites suitable for new or expanded
5 generating stations or energy storage devices, including:
6 (i) brownfields;
7 (ii) industrial sites surrounded by areas with low–population
8 density; and
9 (iii) sites with old or decommissioned generating units that may be
10 repowered or repurposed, with special consideration given to sites with surplus
11 interconnection capacity;
12 (2) identify current bottlenecks and barriers in the State that extend State
13 and local permitting timelines; and
14 (3) develop recommendations on what a State–level zoning or permitting
15 structure should look like in order to promote fast–tracked development at the priority
16 energy sites identified in item (1) of this subsection.
17 (c) On or before December 31, 2026, the Program shall report to the Governor
18 and, in accordance with § 2–1257 of the State Government Article, the General Assembly
19 on the results of the study.
20 SECTION 4. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That this Act shall take effect June
21 1, 2026.
22 SECTION 12. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That Sections 1, 2, 3, 5, 10, and
23 11 of this Act shall take effect July 1, 2026.
24 SECTION 13. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That this Act is an emergency
25 measure, is necessary for the immediate preservation of the public health or safety, has
26 been passed by a yea and nay vote supported by three–fifths of all the members elected to
27 each of the two Houses of the General Assembly, and, except as provided in Section 12 of
28 this Act, shall take effect from the date it is enacted.

1 AN ACT concerning
2 Continuing the Next Generation Energy Act
3 Utility RELIEF (Reducing Energy Load Inflation for Everyday Families) Act
4 FOR the purpose of lowering the maximum monthly energy demand that is required for a
5 certain large load customer to qualify for a specific rate schedule; altering the
6 requirements that a certain multiyear rate plan must meet to be eligible for
7 approval; authorizing the Public Service Commission to require a public service
8 company to include a certain reconciliation procedure in the company’s multiyear
9 rate plan; altering the program cycle for certain energy efficiency and conservation
10 plans; altering the years for which certain electricity savings percentages are used
11 to calculate certain greenhouse gas emissions reduction targets in certain years;
12 prohibiting the Commission from approving a certain energy efficiency and
13 conservation plan that includes a certain residential sector subprogram; altering the
14 definition of “large capacity energy resource” and “zero–emission credit” for
15 provisions relating to energy solicitation and procurement; requiring the
16 Commission to consider, rather than apply, certain costs when calculating certain
17 impacts for certain nuclear energy generation projects; authorizing, with the
18 approval of the Commission, the increase of certain nuclear energy generation
19 project costs under certain circumstances; requiring the Commission to conduct a
20 certain request for information and a certain request for proposals; requiring the
21 Commission to select a certain third–party administrator by a certain date subject
22 to a certain exception; requiring the Power Plant Research Program, in consultation
23 with the Department of the Environment and the Maryland Energy Administration,

17 Article – Local Government
18 1–1320.
19 (a) (1) In this section the following words have the meanings indicated.
20 (2) “Administration” means the Maryland Energy Administration.
21 (3) “Residential energy storage system” means a system, on a residential
22 customer’s side of the meter, used to store electrical energy, or mechanical, chemical, or
23 thermal energy that was once electrical energy, for use as electrical energy at a later date
24 or in a process that offsets electricity use at peak times.
25 (4) “Residential solar energy system” means any configuration of solar
26 energy devices that collects and distributes solar energy for the purpose of generating
27 electricity and that has a single residential interconnection with the electrical grid.
28 (5) “SOLAR PERMITTING FEE” MEANS A FEE EQUAL TO THE SUM OF
29 ALL CHARGES IMPOSED BY A COUNTY OR MUNICIPALITY, INCLUDING CHARGES
30 IMPOSED BY A PROVIDER OF SOLAR PERMITTING SOFTWARE, IN CONNECTION WITH
31 AN APPLICATION FOR A RESIDENTIAL SOLAR ENERGY SYSTEM.
32 (6) “Solar permitting software” means[:

1 (i) the most recent version of a web–based platform, developed by
2 the National Renewable Energy Laboratory, that provides a standard portal for receiving
3 and processing residential solar energy system and residential energy storage system
4 permit information; or
5 (ii) automated software that functions to support the tracking and
6 approval of residential building permits for residential solar energy systems, residential
7 energy storage systems, main electrical panel upgrades, and main electrical panel devices]
8 SOFTWARE OR A COMBINATION OF SOFTWARE THAT:
9 (I) AUTOMATES PLAN REVIEW FOR RESIDENTIAL SOLAR
10 ENERGY SYSTEMS TO THE MOST RECENT VERSION OF, AS APPLICABLE:
11 1. THE MARYLAND BUILDING PERFORMANCE
12 STANDARDS;
13 2. THE NATIONAL ELECTRICAL CODE, INCLUDING

15 3. THE STATE FIRE PREVENTION CODE;
16 (II) PRODUCES CODE–COMPLIANT APPROVALS;
17 (III) ISSUES A CODE–COMPLIANT PERMIT;
18 (IV) ACCEPTS ONLINE PAYMENTS FOR ANY PERMITTING FEES
19 IMPOSED; AND
20 (V) ISSUES PERMITS OR PERMIT REVISIONS IMMEDIATELY ON

25 (a) (1) There is an Environmental Trust Fund.

27 cost of electricity distributed to retail electric customers within the State, an environmental
28 surcharge per kilowatt hour of electric energy distributed in the State to be paid by any
29 electric company as defined in § 1–101 of the Public Utilities Article.
30 (ii) The Public Service Commission shall impose the surcharge per
31 kilowatt hour of electric energy distributed to retail electric customers within the State and
32 shall authorize the electric companies to add the full amount of the surcharge to retail
33 electric customers’ bills.

HOUSE BILL 1532 19
1 (iii) To the extent that the surcharge is not collected from retail
2 electric customers, the surcharge shall be deemed a cost of distribution and shall be allowed
3 and computed as such, together with other allowable expenses, for rate–making purposes.
4 (iv) Revenues from the surcharge shall be collected by the
5 Comptroller and placed in the Fund.
6 (b) (1) (i) The Secretary, in consultation with the Director of the Maryland
7 Energy Administration, annually shall coordinate the preparation of a budget required to
8 carry out the provisions of this subtitle.

10 Service Commission shall establish the amount of the surcharge per kilowatt hour for the
11 fiscal year beginning July 1, 1972, and for each subsequent fiscal year.
12 (2) Notwithstanding any other provisions of this subtitle, the amount of the
13 surcharge for each account for each retail electric customer may not exceed the lesser of
14 0.15 mill per kilowatt hour or $1,000 per month and the surcharge may not continue beyond
15 fiscal year 2030.
16 (3) (i) The Comptroller shall maintain the method of collection of the
17 surcharge from the companies and the collections shall accrue to the Fund.
18 (ii) The Department shall credit against the amount required to be
19 paid into the Environmental Trust Fund by each electric company an amount equal to
20 0.75% of the total surcharge attributed to each company on the basis of the electricity
21 distributed within Maryland.

4 requirements:

11 2. the large load customer agrees to purchase service at that

14 (3) “Large load customer” means a commercial or industrial customer for

17 least [100] 25 megawatts; and
18 (ii) has or is projected to have a load factor of over [80%] 75%.
19 (4) “Load ramp period” means the period of time from commencement of
20 service until a large load customer’s billing calculation is based on the full contract capacity.
21 (b) It is the intent of the General Assembly that residential retail electric
22 customers in the State should not bear the financial risks associated with large load
23 customers interconnecting to the electric system serving the State.

1 (2) protects residential retail electric customers from the financial risks

10 7–321.
11 (A) IN THIS SECTION, “PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM”
12 MEANS A MOVABLE PHOTOVOLTAIC SOLAR ENERGY GENERATION DEVICE THAT IS:
13 (1) DESIGNED TO BE CONNECTED TO A BUILDING’S ELECTRICAL
14 SYSTEM THROUGH A STANDARD ELECTRICAL OUTLET;
15 (2) PRIMARILY INTENDED TO OFFSET PART OF THE BUILDING’S
16 ELECTRICITY CONSUMPTION;
17 (3) LIMITED TO SUPPLYING A MAXIMUM POWER OUTPUT OF NOT
18 MORE THAN 391 WATTS BACK TO THE ELECTRIC SYSTEM OF THE BUILDING; AND
19 (4) CERTIFIED BY UNDERWRITERS LABORATORY OR AN EQUIVALENT
20 NATIONALLY RECOGNIZED TESTING LABORATORY.
21 (B) A PERSON MAY PURCHASE AND INSTALL NOT MORE THAN ONE
22 PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM PER ELECTRIC METER FOR
23 RESIDENTIAL USE ONLY.
24 (C) A PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM:
25 (1) IS NOT SUBJECT TO THE REQUIREMENTS OF §§ 7–306 AND 7–306.1
26 OF THIS SUBTITLE;
27 (2) IS NOT ELIGIBLE FOR INCLUSION IN MEETING THE RENEWABLE
28 ENERGY PORTFOLIO STANDARD; AND
29 (3) MAY NOT GENERATE RENEWABLE ENERGY CREDITS OF ANY TYPE.

HOUSE BILL 1532 57
1 (D) AN ELECTRIC COMPANY:
2 (1) MAY NOT REQUIRE A CUSTOMER USING A PORTABLE SOLAR
3 ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM TO:
4 (I) OBTAIN THE ELECTRIC COMPANY’S APPROVAL BEFORE
5 INSTALLING OR USING THE PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM;
6 (II) PAY ANY FEE OR CHARGE RELATED TO THE PORTABLE
7 SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM’S ABILITY TO FEED ELECTRICITY BACK INTO
8 THE ELECTRIC SYSTEM; OR
9 (III) EXCEPT AS PROVIDED IN SUBSECTION (E) OF THIS SECTION,
10 INSTALL ANY ADDITIONAL CONTROLS OR EQUIPMENT BEYOND WHAT IS
11 INTEGRATED INTO THE PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM; AND
12 (2) IS NOT LIABLE FOR ANY DAMAGE CAUSED BY A PORTABLE SOLAR
13 ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM.
14 (E) A CUSTOMER USING A PORTABLE SOLAR ENERGY GENERATING SYSTEM
15 SHALL:
16 (1) NOTIFY THE ELECTRIC COMPANY PROVIDING SERVICE IN THE
17 SERVICE TERRITORY IN WHICH THE GENERATING SYSTEM WILL BE INSTALLED ONCE
18 THE GENERATING SYSTEM IS INSTALLED;
19 (2) PROVIDE TO THE ELECTRIC COMPANY PROVIDING SERVICE IN
20 THE SERVICE TERRITORY IN WHICH THE GENERATING SYSTEM WILL BE OR IS
21 INSTALLED A CERTIFICATION OF THE SAFETY FEATURES AND MAXIMUM
22 GENERATING CAPACITY OF THE GENERATING SYSTEM; AND
23 (3) IF THE GENERATING SYSTEM REQUIRES AN AUTOMATIC LOCKING
24 DISCONNECT SWITCH TO BE INSTALLED, PAY FOR THE SWITCH INSTALLATION.

17 ADMINISTRATION TO SOLICIT A SERIES OF BIDS FROM RENEWABLE ENERGY
18 PROJECT DEVELOPERS FOR THE DEVELOPMENT OF RENEWABLE ENERGY
19 GENERATION PROJECTS THAT ARE NEEDED TO MEET ELECTRICITY DEMAND IN A
20 COST–EFFECTIVE MANNER.
21 (C) (1) TO BE ELIGIBLE TO SUBMIT A BID UNDER THIS SECTION, A
22 PERSON MUST:
23 (I) BE A RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT
24 DEVELOPER; AND
25 (II) MEET THE MINIMUM CREDIT AND OTHER ELIGIBILITY
26 REQUIREMENTS SET UNDER PARAGRAPH (2) OF THIS SUBSECTION.
27 (2) THE ADMINISTRATION, IN CONSULTATION WITH THE
28 COMMISSION, SHALL SET ELIGIBILITY REQUIREMENTS FOR BIDDERS, INCLUDING
29 REQUIRING EACH BIDDER TO:
30 (I) PROVIDE PROOF OF FINANCIAL INTEGRITY;

HOUSE BILL 1532 75
1 (II) POST A BOND OR OTHER SIMILAR INSTRUMENT;
2 (III) AGREE TO BE SUBJECT TO ALL APPLICABLE TAXES; AND
3 (IV) COMPLY WITH ANY OTHER REQUIREMENTS THE
4 ADMINISTRATION DETERMINES ARE IN THE PUBLIC INTEREST.
5 (D) (1) ELIGIBLE BIDDERS SHALL SUBMIT COMPETITIVE BIDS BY
6 SPECIFYING:
7 (I) THE ACTUAL AMOUNT OF MEGAWATTS TO BE GENERATED
8 BY THE RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT; AND
9 (II) A PRICE PER MEGAWATT THAT WOULD BE REQUIRED FROM
10 THE AUCTION.
11 (2) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL RANK BIDS FROM LOWEST TO
12 HIGHEST COST PER MEGAWATT AND AWARD FUNDS DERIVED FROM ALTERNATIVE
13 COMPLIANCE FEES TO THE LOWEST BID OR BIDS.
14 (3) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL AWARD BIDS UNTIL THE CAPACITY
15 TARGET SET UNDER SUBSECTION (A)(2) OF THIS SECTION IS REACHED.
16 (4) THE BIDDER WHO SUBMITS THE LOWEST RESPONSIVE BID FOR
17 DEVELOPING A RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT SHALL BE AWARDED
18 THE AMOUNT OF FUNDS TO BUILD THE RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT.
19 (5) THE ADMINISTRATION MAY REFUSE TO ACCEPT SOME OR ALL OF
20 THE BIDS MADE IN A COMPETITIVE AUCTION IN ACCORDANCE WITH STANDARDS
21 ADOPTED BY THE ADMINISTRATION.
22 (6) (I) IF THE CAPACITY TARGET CAN BE MET AT A COST BELOW
23 THE ALLOCATED FUNDING, THE ADMINISTRATION MAY:
24 1. CARRY FORWARD ANY FUNDING TO THE NEXT
25 AUCTION, IF APPLICABLE; OR
26 2. APPLY THE FUNDS FOR ANY ADDITIONAL MEGAWATTS
27 OF RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION THAT HAVE BEEN OFFERED UNDER THE
28 AUCTION.
29 (II) ANY AMOUNT OF ALLOCATED FUNDING THAT IS NOT
30 CARRIED FORWARD OR APPLIED UNDER SUBPARAGRAPH (I) OF THIS PARAGRAPH

76 HOUSE BILL 1532
1 SHALL ACCRUE IN THE MARYLAND STRATEGIC ENERGY INVESTMENT FUND AND
2 MAY BE ALLOCATED FOR ANY PURPOSE FOR WHICH ALTERNATIVE COMPLIANCE FEE
3 REVENUE IS AUTHORIZED TO BE USED.
4 (E) (1) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL SET DELIVERY DEADLINES FOR
5 EACH RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT THAT IS AWARDED FUNDING
6 FROM AN AUCTION.
7 (2) THE DEADLINES SET IN PARAGRAPH (1) OF THIS SUBSECTION
8 SHALL INCLUDE MILESTONES THAT REQUIRE THE DEVELOPER TO MEET CERTAIN
9 DELIVERY GOALS DURING THE DEVELOPMENT OF A RENEWABLE ENERGY
10 GENERATION PROJECT.
11 (3) THE ADMINISTRATION MAY GRANT EXTENSIONS FOR DELIVERY
12 GOALS THAT ARE DELAYED DUE TO INTERCONNECTION OR PERMITTING
13 CHALLENGES OR DELAYS IF THE DEVELOPER PROVIDES DOCUMENTATION OF THE
14 CHALLENGE OR DELAY.
15 (4) THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL ESTABLISH A METHOD OF
16 COLLECTION AGAINST ANY DEVELOPER AWARDED A CONTRACT UNDER THIS
17 SECTION TO RECAPTURE ANY FUNDS RECEIVED AS A RESULT OF:
18 (I) MISAPPROPRIATION, OVERPAYMENT, OR FRAUD; OR
19 (II) FAILURE TO MEET MILESTONES OR DELIVERY DATES.
20 (F) WITHIN 90 DAYS AFTER ALL CONTRACTS FOR RENEWABLE ENERGY
21 GENERATION PROJECTS ARE EXECUTED, THE ADMINISTRATION SHALL PUBLICLY
22 DISCLOSE THE NAMES OF EACH SUCCESSFUL BIDDER AND THE MEGAWATTS TO BE
23 DELIVERED BY THE DEVELOPMENT OF THE RENEWABLE ENERGY GENERATION
24 PROJECT.
25 (G) ON OR BEFORE JULY 1, 2027, AND JULY 1, 2028, THE ADMINISTRATION
26 AND THE COMMISSION SHALL REPORT TO THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY, IN
27 ACCORDANCE WITH § 2–1257 OF THIS ARTICLE, ON THE ADMINISTRATION OF THE
28 IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING AUCTION, INCLUDING:
29 (1) THE AMOUNT OF MEGAWATTS PROCURED THROUGH THE
30 AUCTION;
31 (2) THE COST PER MEGAWATT OF RENEWABLE ENERGY ALLOCATED
32 IN THE AUCTION;

HOUSE BILL 1532 77
1 (3) THE NUMBER OF RENEWABLE ENERGY CREDITS CREATED AS A
2 RESULT OF THE AUCTION; AND
3 (4) ANY OTHER INFORMATION THE ADMINISTRATION AND THE
4 COMMISSION CONSIDER RELEVANT.

7 (a) (1) IN THIS SECTION THE FOLLOWING WORDS HAVE THE MEANINGS

9 (2) (I) “BONUS” MEANS A FORM OF DIRECT OR INDIRECT
10 PAYMENT, CONSIDERATION, OR COMPENSATION THAT IS PAID OR CONVEYED TO AN
11 EMPLOYEE OF A PUBLIC SERVICE COMPANY IN ADDITION TO THE EMPLOYEE’S BASE
12 PAY.
13 (II) “BONUS” INCLUDES:
14 1. COMPENSATION THAT THE PUBLIC SERVICE
15 COMPANY DOES NOT FORMALLY LABEL AS A BONUS PAYMENT;
16 2. ANY FORM OF INCENTIVE COMPENSATION THE FACT
17 AND AMOUNT OF WHICH IS UNDER THE DISCRETION OF THE PUBLIC SERVICE
18 COMPANY UNTIL A TIME CLOSE TO THE END OF THE PERIOD FOR WHICH THE
19 INCENTIVE PAYMENT IS PAID; AND
20 3. PAYMENTS GIVEN IN ADDITION TO BASE PAY THAT
21 ARE CONTINGENT ON THE OCCURRENCE OF ONE OR MORE EVENTS OR CONDITIONS.
22 (3) (I) “COMPENSATION” MEANS A FORM OF PAYMENT OR

24 SERVICE COMPANY, THE PARENT COMPANY OF A PUBLIC SERVICE COMPANY, OR ANY
25 OTHER AFFILIATE OF A PUBLIC SERVICE COMPANY IN CONNECTION WITH THE

19 (B) IT IS THE INTENT OF THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY TO TRANSITION TO A NET
20 ENERGY METERING PROGRAM THAT:
21 (1) INCREASES BENEFITS TO RATEPAYERS BY LOWERING ELECTRIC
22 SYSTEM COSTS THROUGH THE USE OF FLEXIBLE CUSTOMER–SITED RENEWABLE
23 ENERGY RESOURCES;
24 (2) PROVIDES FAIR COMPENSATION TO ELIGIBLE
25 CUSTOMER–GENERATORS;
26 (3) IS DESIGNED TO MAKE PROGRESS TOWARD MEETING THE STATE’S
27 DEMAND–SIDE, ENERGY STORAGE, AND CLEAN ENERGY GOALS; AND
28 (4) PROVIDES INCENTIVES FOR THE DEVELOPMENT OF DISTRIBUTED
29 GENERATION THAT ARE LESS THAN THE INCENTIVES PROVIDED BY THE NET ENERGY
30 METERING PROGRAM UNDER § 7–306 OF THIS SUBTITLE.

18 established by regulation under this section a quantity of zero–emission credits equal to
19 the electric company’s respective percentage of retail electric sales each year.
20 (2) Subject to any escrow account reserve requirement the Commission
21 establishes, if there are insufficient zero–emission credits available to satisfy the electric
22 companies’ zero–emission credit purchase obligations, the overpayment shall be distributed
23 to electric companies to be refunded or credited to each distribution customer based on the
24 customer’s consumption of electricity supply that is subject to the renewable energy
25 portfolio standard.
26 (d) A debt, an obligation, or a liability of a nuclear energy generation project or of
27 an owner or operator of a nuclear energy generation project may not be considered a debt,
28 an obligation, or a liability of the State.
29 (E) (1) SUBJECT TO PARAGRAPH (2) OF THIS SUBSECTION, THE
30 COMMISSION MAY APPROVE AN INCREASE OF THE TOTAL COST OF A NUCLEAR
31 ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT UNDER A LONG–TERM PRICING PURCHASE
32 OBLIGATION.
33 (2) THE TOTAL COST OF A NUCLEAR ENERGY GENERATION PROJECT
34 UNDER A LONG–TERM PRICING PURCHASE OBLIGATION MAY NOT BE INCREASED BY
35 MORE THAN 15% OF THE ORIGINAL COST.

HOUSE BILL 1532 103
1 SECTION 2. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
2 (a) (1) On or before July 1, 2026, the Public Service Commission shall issue a
3 request for information on the use of a third–party, single–implementer program for the
4 administration of the programs and services under Title 7, Subtitle 2, Part II of the Public
5 Utilities Article.
6 (2) The request for information shall seek:
7 (i) determinations of what effect the use of a single, third–party
8 administrator would have on costs;
9 (ii) identification of technical and logistical barriers to transitioning
10 to a single, third–party administrator; and
11 (iii) an analysis of the advantages and disadvantages of a private,
12 third–party administrator as opposed to a State administrator.
13 (3) The request for information shall specify a completion date of July 1,
14 2027.
15 (b) (1) Within 30 days after receiving the information requested in subsection
16 (a) of this section, the Public Service Commission shall issue a request for proposals for a
17 third–party administrator for the programs and services under Title 7, Subtitle 2, Part II
18 of the Public Utilities Article.
19 (2) The request for proposals shall specify that responses to the request
20 should minimize short–term and long–term costs for utility ratepayers.
21 (c) (1) Except as provided in paragraph (2) of this subsection, on or before June
22 1, 2028, the Public Service Commission shall select, through the request for proposals
23 process initiated under subsection (b) of this section, a third–party administrator for the
24 administration of the programs and services under Title 7, Subtitle 2, Part II of the Public
25 Utilities Article.
26 (2) (i) The Public Service Commission may decline to select a
27 third–party administrator if the Public Service Commission determines that the use of a
28 third–party administrator would not be cost effective.
29 (ii) The Public Service Commission shall notify the General
30 Assembly of a decision to decline to select a third–party administrator within 5 days after
31 making the decision.
32 SECTION 3. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
33 (a) The Power Plant Research Program, in consultation with the Department of
34 the Environment and the Maryland Energy Administration, shall conduct a study to

104 HOUSE BILL 1532
1 identify ways to streamline the permitting process for energy development in the State.
2 (b) In conducting the study under subsection (a) of this section, the Power Plant
3 Research Program shall:
4 (1) identify up to 50 priority energy sites suitable for new or expanded
5 generating stations or energy storage devices, including:
6 (i) brownfields;
7 (ii) industrial sites surrounded by areas with low–population
8 density; and
9 (iii) sites with old or decommissioned generating units that may be
10 repowered or repurposed, with special consideration given to sites with surplus
11 interconnection capacity;
12 (2) identify current bottlenecks and barriers in the State that extend State
13 and local permitting timelines; and
14 (3) develop recommendations on what a State–level zoning or permitting
15 structure should look like in order to promote fast–tracked development at the priority
16 energy sites identified in item (1) of this subsection.
17 (c) On or before December 31, 2026, the Program shall report to the Governor
18 and, in accordance with § 2–1257 of the State Government Article, the General Assembly
19 on the results of the study.
20 SECTION 4. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That this Act shall take effect June
21 1, 2026.
22 SECTION 12. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That Sections 1, 2, 3, 5, 10, and
23 11 of this Act shall take effect July 1, 2026.
24 SECTION 13. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That this Act is an emergency
25 measure, is necessary for the immediate preservation of the public health or safety, has
26 been passed by a yea and nay vote supported by three–fifths of all the members elected to
27 each of the two Houses of the General Assembly, and, except as provided in Section 12 of
28 this Act, shall take effect from the date it is enacted.
